<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_appointments">Judicial appointments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_K._Polk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Judicial appointments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Cooper_Grier_-_Brady-Handy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Robert_Cooper_Grier_-_Brady-Handy.jpg/175px-Robert_Cooper_Grier_-_Brady-Handy.jpg" width="175" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Robert_Cooper_Grier_-_Brady-Handy.jpg/263px-Robert_Cooper_Grier_-_Brady-Handy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Robert_Cooper_Grier_-_Brady-Handy.jpg/350px-Robert_Cooper_Grier_-_Brady-Handy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3144" data-file-height="3872" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Cooper_Grier_-_Brady-Handy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Robert_Cooper_Grier" title="Robert Cooper Grier">Robert Cooper Grier</a>, one of President Polk's two appointees to the Supreme Court.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_federal_judges_appointed_by_James_K._Polk" title="List of federal judges appointed by James K. Polk">List of federal judges appointed by James K. Polk</a></div>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Supreme_Court">Supreme Court</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_K._Polk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Supreme Court">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Polk appointed the following Justices to the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">U.S. Supreme Court</a>:</p>
<table class="sortable wikitable">
<tr bgcolor="#ECECEC">
<td><b>Justice</b></td>
<td><b>Position</b></td>
<td><b>Began active<br />
service</b></td>
<td><b>Ended active<br />
service</b></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Levi_Woodbury" title="Levi Woodbury">Levi Woodbury</a></td>
<td>Seat 2</td>
<td><span style="display:none">18450920</span>September 20, 1845<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></td>
<td><span style="display:none">18510904</span>September 4, 1851</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Robert_Cooper_Grier" title="Robert Cooper Grier">Robert Cooper Grier</a></td>
<td>Seat 3</td>
<td><span style="display:none">18460804</span>August 4, 1846</td>
<td><span style="display:none">18700131</span>January 31, 1870</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Polk nominated both <a href="/wiki/George_W._Woodward" class="mw-redirect" title="George W. Woodward">George W. Woodward</a> of Pennsylvania and Levi Woodbury of New Hampshire in December 1845. Woodbury was confirmed, but Woodward was rejected by the Senate in 1846. Woodward's nomination was defeated in large part due to the opposition of Buchanan and Pennsylvania Senator <a href="/wiki/Simon_Cameron" title="Simon Cameron">Simon Cameron</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Polk subsequently nominated Robert Cooper Grier of Pennsylvania, and Grier won confirmation. Woodbury died in 1851, but Grier served until 1870 and notably joined with the majority decision in <i><a href="/wiki/Dred_Scott_v._Sandford" title="Dred Scott v. Sandford">Dred Scott v. Sandford</a></i>.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_judicial_appointments">Other judicial appointments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_K._Polk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Other judicial appointments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Polk appointed eight other federal judges, one to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Circuit_Court_of_the_District_of_Columbia" title="United States Circuit Court of the District of Columbia">United States Circuit Court of the District of Columbia</a>, and seven to various <a href="/wiki/United_States_district_court" title="United States district court">United States district courts</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_policy">Foreign policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_K._Polk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Foreign policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Polk strongly supported expansion, and relations with Mexico and Great Britain, the country's southern and northern neighbors respectively, dominated Polk's presidency. Polk, like many other Democrats, fervently believed in the idea of <a href="/wiki/Manifest_Destiny" class="mw-redirect" title="Manifest Destiny">Manifest Destiny</a>, and he sought to create a bicoastal nation. Polk was successful in pursuing this goal, as his presidency saw the partition of <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Country" title="Oregon Country">Oregon Country</a> with Britain, the annexation of Texas, and the acquisition of vast amounts of land from Mexico.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Partition_of_Oregon_Country">Partition of Oregon Country</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_K._Polk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Partition of Oregon Country">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oregon_boundary_dispute" title="Oregon boundary dispute">Oregon boundary dispute</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oregoncountry2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Oregoncountry2.png/290px-Oregoncountry2.png" width="290" height="296" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Oregoncountry2.png/435px-Oregoncountry2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Oregoncountry2.png/580px-Oregoncountry2.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1019" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oregoncountry2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Country" title="Oregon Country">Oregon Country</a>, which the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Treaty" title="Oregon Treaty">Oregon Treaty</a> split between the Americans and British at the 49th parallel</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_1818" title="Treaty of 1818">Treaty of 1818</a>, the Oregon Country had been under the joint occupation and control of the United Kingdom and the United States. Previous U.S. administrations had offered to divide the region along the <a href="/wiki/49th_parallel_north" title="49th parallel north">49th parallel</a>, which was not acceptable to Britain, as they had commercial interests along the <a href="/wiki/Columbia_River" title="Columbia River">Columbia River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-merry168169_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry168169-84">[84]</a></sup> Britain's preferred partition was unacceptable to Polk, as it would have awarded the <a href="/wiki/Puget_Sound" title="Puget Sound">Puget Sound</a> and all lands North of the Columbia River to Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-merry168169_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry168169-84">[84]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edward_Everett" title="Edward Everett">Edward Everett</a>, President Tyler's ambassador to Great Britain, had proposed a new solution that would divide most of the territory at the 49th parallel but grant the strategic <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Island" title="Vancouver Island">Vancouver Island</a> to the British, but Tyler's term ended before negotiations could proceed.<sup id="cite_ref-merry170171_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry170171-85">[85]</a></sup> Though both sides sought an acceptable compromise, each also saw the territory as an important geopolitical asset that would play a large part in determining the dominant power in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-merry168169_84-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry168169-84">[84]</a></sup> On taking office, Polk announced that he viewed the American claim to the land as "clear and unquestionable," provoking threats of war from British leaders should Polk attempt to take control of the entire territory.<sup id="cite_ref-merry170171_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry170171-85">[85]</a></sup> Despite Polk's hawkish rhetoric and desire to annex the entire territory, he viewed war with the British as unwise and unnecessary, and Polk and Buchanan opened up negotiations with the British.<sup id="cite_ref-merry173175_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry173175-86">[86]</a></sup> Like his predecessors, Polk again proposed a division along the 49th parallel, which was immediately rejected by the British ambassador, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Pakenham" title="Richard Pakenham">Richard Pakenham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Secretary of State Buchanan was wary of a two-front war with both Mexico and Britain, but Polk was willing to risk war with both countries in pursuit of a favorable settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-merry190191_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry190191-88">[88]</a></sup> As 1845 came to an end, Polk began preparations to give Britain a one-year notice (as required in the Treaty of 1818) of his intention to terminate the joint occupancy of Oregon.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>When the British Foreign Secretary, <a href="/wiki/George_Hamilton-Gordon,_4th_Earl_of_Aberdeen" title="George Hamilton-Gordon, 4th Earl of Aberdeen">Lord Aberdeen</a>, learned of the proposal rejected by Pakenham, Aberdeen asked the United States to re-open negotiations.<sup id="cite_ref-merry196197_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry196197-90">[90]</a></sup> After the brief collapse of British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Robert_Peel" title="Robert Peel">Robert Peel</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Second_Peel_ministry" title="Second Peel ministry">second ministry</a>, Peel and Aberdeen sought closer relations with the United States as part of a re-orientation towards free trade.<sup id="cite_ref-merry224225_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry224225-91">[91]</a></sup> In March 1846, Polk allowed Buchanan to inform <a href="/wiki/Louis_McLane" title="Louis McLane">Louis McLane</a>, the American ambassador to Britain, that Polk's administration would look favorably on a British proposal based around a division at the 49th parallel.<sup id="cite_ref-merry225227_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry225227-92">[92]</a></sup> In June 1846, Pakenham presented an offer to the Polk administration, calling for a boundary line at the 49th parallel, with the exception that Britain would retain all of Vancouver Island, and limited navigation rights for British subjects on the Columbia River.<sup id="cite_ref-merry263264_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry263264-93">[93]</a></sup> Polk and most of his Cabinet were prepared to accept the proposal, but Buchanan, in a surprising reversal, urged that the United States seek control of all of the Oregon Territory.<sup id="cite_ref-merry263264_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry263264-93">[93]</a></sup> After winning the reluctant approval of Buchanan and many of Polk's Senate allies, Polk submitted the full treaty to the Senate for ratification.<sup id="cite_ref-merry266267_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry266267-94">[94]</a></sup> The Senate ratified the treaty in a 41–14 vote.<sup id="cite_ref-merry266267_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry266267-94">[94]</a></sup> After years of negotiations, the United States and Great Britain had finally settled the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_boundary_dispute" title="Oregon boundary dispute">Oregon question</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-merry266267_94-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry266267-94">[94]</a></sup> Polk's willingness to risk war with Britain had frightened many, but his tough negotiation tactics may have gained the United States concessions from the British (particularly regarding the Columbia River) that a more conciliatory president might not have won.<sup id="cite_ref-merry266267_94-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry266267-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>The portion of the Oregon Territory acquired by the United States later formed the states of <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Idaho" title="Idaho">Idaho</a>, and parts of the states of <a href="/wiki/Montana" title="Montana">Montana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a>. The borders established by the Oregon Treaty now constitute a portion of the <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="Canada–United States border">Canada–United States border</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Annexation_of_Texas">Annexation of Texas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_K._Polk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Annexation of Texas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Texas_Annexation" class="mw-redirect" title="Texas Annexation">Texas Annexation</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mapa_de_Mexico_1845.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Mapa_de_Mexico_1845.PNG/300px-Mapa_de_Mexico_1845.PNG" width="300" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Mapa_de_Mexico_1845.PNG/450px-Mapa_de_Mexico_1845.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Mapa_de_Mexico_1845.PNG/600px-Mapa_de_Mexico_1845.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1478" data-file-height="1315" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mapa_de_Mexico_1845.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Mexico in 1845, with the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">Republic of Texas</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Yucatan" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Yucatan">Republic of Yucatan</a> and the disputed territory between Mexico and Texas in red. Mexico claimed to own all of Texas.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">Republic of Texas</a> had gained independence from <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> following the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Revolution" title="Texas Revolution">Texas Revolution</a> of 1836. Many <a href="/wiki/Texians" title="Texians">Texians</a> had migrated from the United States, and many Americans and Texians sought to make Texas a part of America following the Texas Revolution. Upon hearing of Polk's election to office, President Tyler had urged Congress to pass a <a href="/wiki/Joint_resolution" title="Joint resolution">joint resolution</a> admitting Texas to the Union, and Congress complied on February 28, 1845. Polk's first major decision in office was whether to recall Tyler's emissary to Texas who bore an offer of annexation based on that act of Congress.<sup id="cite_ref-Merry136137_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Merry136137-95">[95]</a></sup> Though it was within Polk's power to recall the messenger, he chose to allow the emissary to continue, with the hope that Texas would accept the offer.<sup id="cite_ref-Merry136137_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Merry136137-95">[95]</a></sup> Polk also retained the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Ambassador_to_Texas" title="United States Ambassador to Texas">United States Ambassador to Texas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Jackson_Donelson" title="Andrew Jackson Donelson">Andrew Jackson Donelson</a>, who sought to convince the Texan leaders to accept annexation under the terms proposed by the Tyler administration.<sup id="cite_ref-Merry148151_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Merry148151-96">[96]</a></sup> Though public sentiment in Texas favored annexation, some Texas leaders disliked the strict terms for annexation, which offered little leeway for negotiation and gave public lands to the federal government.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> However, in July 1845, a convention in <a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas">Austin, Texas</a> ratified the annexation of Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> In December 1845, Polk signed a resolution annexing Texas, and Texas became the 28th state in the union.<sup id="cite_ref-merry211212_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry211212-99">[99]</a></sup> The annexation of Texas would lead to increased tensions with Mexico, which had never recognized Texan independence.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexican-American_War">Mexican-American War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_K._Polk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Mexican-American War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a></div>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_of_the_war">Origins of the war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_K._Polk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Origins of the war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Perhaps the most important event of Polk's presidency was the <a href="/wiki/Mexican-American_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican-American War">Mexican-American War</a>. Though the United States had been the first country to recognize <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>'s independence following the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence" title="Mexican War of Independence">Mexican War of Independence</a>, relations between the two countries began to sour in the 1830s.<sup id="cite_ref-Merry184186_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Merry184186-100">[100]</a></sup> In the 1830s and 1840s, the United States, like France and Britain, sought a reparations treaty with Mexico for various acts committed by Mexican citizens and authorities, including the seizure of American ships.<sup id="cite_ref-Merry184186_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Merry184186-100">[100]</a></sup> Though the United States and Mexico had agreed to a joint board to settle the various claims prior to Polk's presidency, many Americans accused the Mexican government of acting in bad faith.<sup id="cite_ref-Merry184186_100-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Merry184186-100">[100]</a></sup> For its part, Mexico saw many Americans as desirous of the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">Alta California</a> and of filing specious or exaggerated claims.<sup id="cite_ref-Merry184186_100-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Merry184186-100">[100]</a></sup> The already-troubled <a href="/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Mexico–United States relations">Mexico–United States relations</a> were further inflamed by the possibility of the annexation of Texas, as Mexico still viewed Texas as an integral part of Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-Merry176177_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Merry176177-101">[101]</a></sup> Additionally, Texas laid claim to all land North of the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio Grande River">Rio Grande River</a>, while Mexico argued that the more northern <a href="/wiki/Nueces_River" title="Nueces River">Nueces River</a> was the proper Texan border.<sup id="cite_ref-Merry187_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Merry187-102">[102]</a></sup> Though the United States had a population more than twice as numerous and an economy thirteen times greater than that of Mexico, Mexico was not prepared to give up its claim to Texas, even if it meant war.<sup id="cite_ref-Merry180_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Merry180-103">[103]</a></sup> Following the Texan ratification of annexation in 1845, both Mexicans and Americans saw war as a likely possibility.<sup id="cite_ref-Merry176177_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Merry176177-101">[101]</a></sup> Polk began preparations for a potential war with Mexico over Texas, and Polk sent an army led by General <a href="/wiki/Zachary_Taylor" title="Zachary Taylor">Zachary Taylor</a> into Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-Merry188189_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Merry188189-104">[104]</a></sup> Taylor and Commodore <a href="/wiki/David_Conner_(naval_officer)" title="David Conner (naval officer)">David Conner</a> of the US Navy were both ordered to avoid provoking a war, while at the same time to prepare for war and respond to any Mexican breach of peace.<sup id="cite_ref-Merry188189_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Merry188189-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Polk_proclamation.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Polk_proclamation.gif/220px-Polk_proclamation.gif" width="220" height="344" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Polk_proclamation.gif/330px-Polk_proclamation.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Polk_proclamation.gif/440px-Polk_proclamation.gif 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="937" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Polk_proclamation.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Polk's presidential proclamation of <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">war against Mexico</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Though Polk genuinely desired to avoid a war with Mexico, he more strongly desired the acquisition of Texas and Alta California.<sup id="cite_ref-merry195196_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry195196-105">[105]</a></sup> As in Texas, Mexico had failed to establish strong control over the sprawling expanse of California, and, as in Texas, many Americans had migrated to the region.<sup id="cite_ref-merry199200_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry199200-106">[106]</a></sup> Polk was particularly worried that the British or another European power would eventually establish control over California if it remained in Mexican hands.<sup id="cite_ref-lee1_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lee1-107">[107]</a></sup> Polk hoped that a show of force by the U.S. military under Taylor and Conner could avert war and lead to negotiations with the Mexican government.<sup id="cite_ref-Merry188189_104-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Merry188189-104">[104]</a></sup> In late 1845, Polk sent diplomat <a href="/wiki/John_Slidell" title="John Slidell">John Slidell</a> to Mexico to purchase California for $20–40&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-merry193194_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry193194-108">[108]</a></sup> Slidell arrived in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> in December 1845.<sup id="cite_ref-merry209210_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry209210-109">[109]</a></sup> Though Mexican President <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Joaqu%C3%ADn_de_Herrera" title="José Joaquín de Herrera">José Joaquín de Herrera</a> was open to negotiations, Slidell's ambassadorial credentials were refused by a Mexican council of government.<sup id="cite_ref-merry209210_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry209210-109">[109]</a></sup> In December 1845, Herrera's government collapsed in large part due to his willingness to negotiate with the United States, as the possibility of the sale of large portions of Mexico aroused anger among both the Mexican elites and broader populace.<sup id="cite_ref-merry218219_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry218219-110">[110]</a></sup> Herrera was succeeded by General <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Paredes_(President_of_Mexico)" title="Mariano Paredes (President of Mexico)">Mariano Paredes</a>, and Mexico began to write a new constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-merry218219_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry218219-110">[110]</a></sup> As successful negotiations with the unstable Mexican government appeared unlikely, War Secretary Marcy ordered General Taylor to advance to the Rio Grande River.<sup id="cite_ref-merry218219_110-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry218219-110">[110]</a></sup> Polk began preparations to support a potential new government led by the exiled Mexican General <a href="/wiki/Antonio_L%C3%B3pez_de_Santa_Anna" title="Antonio López de Santa Anna">Antonio López de Santa Anna</a> with the hope that Santa Anna would sell parts of California.<sup id="cite_ref-merry238240_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry238240-111">[111]</a></sup> Polk had been advised by Alejandro Atocha, an associate of Santa Anna, that only the threat of war would allow the Mexican government the leeway to sell parts of Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-merry238240_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry238240-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 1846, Slidell finally left Mexico after the government refused his demand to be formally received.<sup id="cite_ref-merry232233_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry232233-112">[112]</a></sup> Slidell returned to Washington in May 1846, and gave his opinion that negotiations with the Mexican government were unlikely to be successful.<sup id="cite_ref-merry240242_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry240242-113">[113]</a></sup> Polk regarded the treatment of his diplomat as an insult and an "ample cause of war", and he prepared to ask Congress for a declaration of war.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Meanwhile, in late March, General Taylor had reached the Rio Grande, and his army camped across the river from <a href="/wiki/Matamoros,_Tamaulipas" title="Matamoros, Tamaulipas">Matamoros, Tamaulipas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-merry238240_111-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry238240-111">[111]</a></sup> In April, after Mexican general <a href="/wiki/Pedro_de_Ampudia" title="Pedro de Ampudia">Pedro de Ampudia</a> demanded that Taylor return to the Nueces River, Taylor began a blockade of Matamoros.<sup id="cite_ref-merry240242_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry240242-113">[113]</a></sup> A skirmish on the northern side of the Rio Grande ended in the death or capture of dozens of American soldiers, and became known as the <a href="/wiki/Thornton_Affair" title="Thornton Affair">Thornton Affair</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-merry240242_113-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry240242-113">[113]</a></sup> While the administration was in the process of asking for a declaration of war, Polk received word of the outbreak of hostilities on the Rio Grande.<sup id="cite_ref-merry240242_113-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry240242-113">[113]</a></sup> In a message to Congress, Polk explained his decision to send Taylor to the Rio Grande, and stated that Mexico had invaded American territory by crossing the river.<sup id="cite_ref-merry244245_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry244245-115">[115]</a></sup> Polk contended that a state of war already existed, and he asked Congress to grant him the power to bring the war to a close.<sup id="cite_ref-merry244245_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry244245-115">[115]</a></sup> Polk's message was crafted to present the war as a just and necessary defense of the country against a neighbor that had long troubled the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-lee2_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lee2-116">[116]</a></sup> In his message, Polk noted that Slidell had gone to Mexico to negotiate a recognition of the Texas annexation, but did not mention that he also sought the purchase of California.<sup id="cite_ref-lee2_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lee2-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some Whigs, such as <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a>, challenged Polk's version of events,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> but the House overwhelmingly approved of a resolution authorizing the president to call up fifty thousand volunteers.<sup id="cite_ref-merry244246_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry244246-118">[118]</a></sup> In the Senate, war opponents led by Calhoun also questioned Polk's version of events.<sup id="cite_ref-merry246247_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry246247-119">[119]</a></sup> Nonetheless, the House resolution passed the Senate in a 40–2 vote, marking the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Mexican-American_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican-American War">Mexican-American War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-merry246247_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry246247-119">[119]</a></sup> Many would-be opponents of the war feared that opposition would cost them politically by casting themselves as unpatriotic for not supporting the war effort.<sup id="cite_ref-merry244245_115-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merry244245-115">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Course_of_the_war">Course of the war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_K._Polk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Course of the war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mexican%E2%80%93American_War_(without_Scott%27s_Campaign)-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War_%28without_Scott%27s_Campaign%29-en.svg/450px-Mexican%E2%80%93American_War_%28without_Scott%27s_Campaign%29-en.svg.png" width="450" height="386" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War_%28without_Scott%27s_Campaign%29-en.svg/675px-Mexican%E2%80%93American_War_%28without_Scott%27s_Campaign%29-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War_%28without_Scott%27s_Campaign%29-en.svg/900px-Mexican%E2%80%93American_War_%28without_Scott%27s_Campaign%29-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1433" data-file-height="1230" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mexican%E2%80%93American_War_(without_Scott%27s_Campaign)-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>

<div>

<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #EFE0C7; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;United States territory, 1848</div>
